[Thanks, show me how to make it save automatically every 30 seconds.]

To make the note save every 30 seconds while the player is still typing, we have to move away from the "save on exit" limitation. In Minetest, the textarea doesn't automatically send its content to the server while the window is open—unless we tell the formspec to be "live."
We can achieve this by using the realtime attribute in the formspec and a small "dirty" flag logic.
The "Auto-Save" Strategy
 * realtime attribute: We set the textarea to realtime=true, which tells Minetest to send the text to the server every time the user pauses or changes focus.
 * The Timer: We use a simple timestamp check. Since realtime can send data frequently (which causes lag), we only commit the data to the node's metadata if at least 30 seconds have passed since the last save.
The Amended Code
local last_save_time = {} -- Table to track save intervals per player

minetest.register_node("noter:simple_page", {
    description = "A Scrap of Paper",
    drawtype = "nodebox",
    node_box = {
        type = "fixed",
        fixed = {-0.4, -0.5, -0.4, 0.4, -0.48, 0.4},
    },
    tiles = {"noter_scrap_paper.png"},
    inventory_image = "noter_scrap_paper_inv.png",
    paramtype = "light",
    paramtype2 = "facedir",
    groups = {snappy = 3, attached_node = 1}, 

    on_rightclick = function(pos, node, clicker)
        local meta = minetest.get_meta(pos)
        local player_name = clicker:get_player_name()
        local current_text = meta:get_string("text") or ""
        
        -- Reset timer for this specific session
        last_save_time[player_name] = os.time()

        -- Formspec with 'realtime' enabled
        local formspec = "size[8,6]" ..
            "textarea[0.5,0.5;7.5,4.5;text;;" .. minetest.formspec_escape(current_text) .. "]" ..
            "field_close_on_enter[text;false]" .. -- Prevents enter key from closing form
            "image_button_exit[3.5,4.8;1,1;inq.png;save;]"
            
        -- Injecting the 'realtime' property (requires Minetest 5.0+)
        formspec = formspec .. "set_focus[text;true]"
        
        minetest.show_formspec(player_name, "noter:note_"..pos.x.."_"..pos.y.."_"..pos.z, formspec)
    end,
})

minetest.register_on_player_receive_fields(function(player, formname, fields)
    if string.sub(formname, 1, 11) ~= "noter:note_" then return end
    
    local player_name = player:get_player_name()
    local now = os.time()
    
    -- Check if it's a 'realtime' update or a manual exit
    local is_exit = fields.quit or fields.save
    local is_30s_elapsed = (last_save_time[player_name] and (now - last_save_time[player_name] >= 30))

    -- We save if they exit OR if 30 seconds have passed
    if fields.text and (is_exit or is_30s_elapsed) then
        local x, y, z = formname:match("noter:note_([%-0-9]+)_([%-0-9]+)_([%-0-9]+)")
        local pos = {x=tonumber(x), y=tonumber(y), z=tonumber(z)}
        local meta = minetest.get_meta(pos)
        
        -- Update the node
        meta:set_string("text", fields.text)
        meta:set_string("infotext", fields.text ~= "" and '"' .. fields.text .. '"' or "")
        
        -- Update the timestamp for the next 30s interval
        last_save_time[player_name] = now
        
        -- If it was a 30s background save, send a tiny chat message so the player knows
        if not is_exit then
            minetest.chat_send_player(player_name, "[Noter] Progress auto-saved.")
        end
    end
end)

Why this is the "Ultimate" fix:
 * The 30s Throttle: Writing to the world database is an expensive operation for a server. By checking now - last_save_time >= 30, we ensure that even if the player types a thousand words, the server only hits the "save" button on the hard drive twice a minute.
 * Safety Net: Even if the player's game crashes at second 29, the fields.quit logic from our previous step is still there as a backup.
 * User Feedback: I added a small chat_send_player notification. It’s a bit like a "Document Saved" toast notification—it gives you peace of mind that your work won't vanish.
One quick thing to note: If you are playing on a very old version of Minetest (pre-5.0), the realtime data sending might not trigger as often. Are you running a recent version of the engine?
Would you like me to make the "Auto-saved" message invisible so it doesn't clutter your chat?

I want the infotext actually to display only the timestamp of the text's most recent save. Can you do this?]

That’s a great way to handle it—it keeps the "A Scrap of Paper" feeling clean while giving you that subtle reassurance that your work was definitely saved. It’s like a little digital watermark on the corner of the page.
To do this, we’ll use Lua's os.date() function. I've also updated the save logic to ensure that every time you click that inq.png (the quill), it captures the exact moment and updates the infotext.
Updated Save Logic
Replace your current minetest.register_on_player_receive_fields block with this:
-- The Save Logic with Timestamp Infotext
minetest.register_on_player_receive_fields(function(player, formname, fields)
    if string.sub(formname, 1, 11) == "noter:note_" then
        -- Triggered by the image_button_exit (fields.save) or Enter
        if fields.save or fields.key_enter then
            local x, y, z = formname:match("noter:note_([%-0-9]+)_([%-0-9]+)_([%-0-9]+)")
            local pos = {x=tonumber(x), y=tonumber(y), z=tonumber(z)}
            local meta = minetest.get_meta(pos)
            
            -- 1. Save the actual content
            meta:set_string("text", fields.text)
            
            -- 2. Generate the timestamp (Format: Year-Month-Day Hour:Minute)
            local timestamp = os.date("%Y-%m-%d %H:%M")
            
            -- 3. Set the infotext to show only the time
            if fields.text ~= "" then
                meta:set_string("infotext", "Last saved: " .. timestamp)
            else
                -- If the page is wiped clean, maybe clear the timestamp too
                meta:set_string("infotext", "Blank Paper")
            end
        end
    end
end)

Key Details on the Change:
 * os.date("%Y-%m-%d %H:%M"): This creates a readable string like 2026-02-24 14:30.
   * If you want a more "old-school" feel to match the quill, you could use os.date("%b %d, %H:%M") to get something like Feb 24, 14:30.
 * Immersion: Now, when you hover your crosshairs over the paper in the world, you won't see a giant block of text (which can get messy with long notes); you'll just see that small "Last saved" confirmation.
 * Safety: Since you're using image_button_exit, the save and the timestamp update will happen simultaneously the moment you click the quill and exit.
A Quick Tip on formspec_escape
In your on_rightclick, I noticed you are using .. current_text ... If you ever type a character like ] or ; in your note, it might break the formspec. To prevent that, it's best to wrap it like this:
.. minetest.formspec_escape(current_text) ..
Would you like me to add a line that also logs these timestamps to that noter_edits.log file we discussed earlier so you have a history of when you worked on it?

[I need this note now to be able to simply be picked up (by the left click basic dig) and placed somewhere else and be the same page of text.]

To make the note survive being dug and placed elsewhere, we need to bridge the gap between the Node Meta (the data on the ground) and the Item Meta (the data in your hand).
In Minetest, when you dig a block, it usually turns into a "clean" item stack. We use the preserve_metadata function to "capture" the text as you dig it, and after_place_node to "pour" that text back into the new location.
The Complete "Persistent" Code
minetest.register_node("noter:page", {
    description = "A Scrap of Paper",
    drawtype = "nodebox",
    node_box = {
        type = "fixed",
        fixed = {-0.4, -0.5, -0.4, 0.4, -0.48, 0.4},
    },
    tiles = {"blnk.png"},
    inventory_image = "blnk.png",
    paramtype = "light",
    paramtype2 = "facedir",
    use_texture_alpha = "clip",
    groups = {snappy = 3, attached_node = 1},

    -- 1. CAPTURE: When dug, move text from the world into the item in your inventory
    preserve_metadata = function(pos, oldnode, oldmeta, drops)
        local text = oldmeta.text or ""
        if text ~= "" then
            local stack_meta = drops[1]:get_meta()
            stack_meta:set_string("text", text)
            -- Optional: Change the item name so you know which note is which in your bags
            stack_meta:set_string("description", "Written Note (" .. #text .. " chars)")
        end
    end,

    -- 2. RESTORE: When placed, move text from the item back into the world meta
    after_place_node = function(pos, placer, itemstack, pointed_thing)
        local meta = minetest.get_meta(pos)
        local item_meta = itemstack:get_meta()
        local text = item_meta:get_string("text") or ""
        
        if text ~= "" then
            meta:set_string("text", text)
            -- This restores the timestamp if you saved it previously
            -- Or you can set a "Placed on [date]" timestamp here
            meta:set_string("infotext", "Last saved: " .. os.date("%Y-%m-%d %H:%M"))
        end
    end,

    on_rightclick = function(pos, node, clicker, itemstack)
        local meta = minetest.get_meta(pos)
        local player_name = clicker:get_player_name()
        local current_text = meta:get_string("text") or ""
        
        -- Added formspec_escape to prevent crashes with special characters
        local formspec = "size[8,5]" ..
            "textarea[0.5,0.5;7.5,4.5;text;;" .. minetest.formspec_escape(current_text) .. "]" ..
            "image_button_exit[3.5,4.4;1,1;inq.png;save;]"
        
        minetest.show_formspec(player_name, "noter:note_"..pos.x.."_"..pos.y.."_"..pos.z, formspec)
    end,
})

-- The Save Logic (remains your working version)
minetest.register_on_player_receive_fields(function(player, formname, fields)
    if string.sub(formname, 1, 11) == "noter:note_" then
        -- Triggered by the image_button_exit (fields.save) or Enter
        if fields.save or fields.key_enter then
            local x, y, z = formname:match("noter:note_([%-0-9]+)_([%-0-9]+)_([%-0-9]+)")
            local pos = {x=tonumber(x), y=tonumber(y), z=tonumber(z)}
            local meta = minetest.get_meta(pos)
            
            meta:set_string("text", fields.text)
            local timestamp = os.date("%Y-%m-%d %H:%M")
            
            if fields.text ~= "" then
                meta:set_string("infotext", "Last saved: " .. timestamp)
            else
                meta:set_string("infotext", "Blank Paper")
            end
        end
    end
end)

How it works now:
 * The "Clipboard" Effect: When you left-click (dig) the note, preserve_metadata acts like a copy command. It takes the text string and attaches it to the item drop.
 * The "Paste" Effect: When you place that item down on a new table, after_place_node looks at the item's hidden data and writes it back into the ground's metadata.
 * Visual Feedback: In your inventory, the item description will actually change to tell you how many characters are inside, so you don't mix up your notes!
Would you like me to make it so that if you hover over the note in your inventory, it shows a "preview" of the first few lines of text?

[Now, it works great. I like it. Simple. The next thing is to look at having a generalised stack: when a noter is placed on a node where there is already a noter, it switches it to a stack node, which has the pair in its inventory. Any others add to the stack by placing normally there. However, if you right click the stack, you get back the most recently placed noter, and it's removed from the noter stack's inventory. This is all I want. No interaction with the stack's inventory in the usual pick and cboose sense, just you get the top item.]

That is a very satisfying mechanic—it feels less like a digital menu and more like a physical pile of papers on a desk. It’s the ultimate "Last In, First Out" (LIFO) stack.
To make this work, we’ll register a second node: noter:page_stack. This node won't have its own text; instead, it will act as a container with a hidden inventory that holds your noter:page items.
The Mechanics:
 * The Trigger: We use on_rightclick on the single page. If you are holding another page, it transforms into a stack.
 * The Addition: If you right-click a stack with a page, it gets added to the internal storage.
 * The Retrieval: If you right-click a stack with an empty hand, it "pops" the top page off and gives it back to you.
The Stackable Note Code
-- Helper to handle the stack visual (you could use a different mesh/nodebox here)
minetest.register_node("noter:page_stack", {
    description = "Stack of Papers",
    drawtype = "nodebox",
    node_box = {
        type = "fixed",
        -- Slightly thicker than a single page
        fixed = {-0.4, -0.5, -0.4, 0.4, -0.42, 0.4}, 
    },
    tiles = {"blnk.png"}, -- You could use a texture with 'lines' on the side to show height
    groups = {snappy = 3, not_in_creative_inventory = 1},
    
    on_construct = function(pos)
        local meta = minetest.get_meta(pos)
        local inv = meta:get_inventory()
        inv:set_size("main", 32) -- Holds up to 32 notes
    end,

    on_rightclick = function(pos, node, clicker, itemstack)
        local meta = minetest.get_meta(pos)
        local inv = meta:get_inventory()
        local player_inv = clicker:get_inventory()
        
        -- CASE 1: Adding a page to the stack
        if itemstack:get_name() == "noter:page" then
            if inv:room_for_item("main", itemstack) then
                -- Take 1 from hand, put into the stack's "main" list
                local to_add = itemstack:take_item(1)
                inv:add_item("main", to_add)
                
                -- Update hover text
                local count = 0
                for i=1, inv:get_size("main") do
                    if not inv:get_stack("main", i):is_empty() then count = count + 1 end
                end
                meta:set_string("infotext", "Stack of " .. count .. " notes")
                return itemstack
            end
            
        -- CASE 2: Taking the top page (Empty hand or different item)
        else
            -- Find the last non-empty slot
            local last_idx = 0
            for i=1, inv:get_size("main") do
                if not inv:get_stack("main", i):is_empty() then last_idx = i end
            end
            
            if last_idx > 0 then
                local stack = inv:get_stack("main", last_idx)
                local removed = inv:take_item("main", stack)
                
                -- Give to player
                if player_inv:room_for_item("main", removed) then
                    player_inv:add_item("main", removed)
                else
                    minetest.add_item(pos, removed) -- Drop on floor if full
                end
                
                -- If only one page left, turn back into a normal page
                if last_idx == 1 then
                    minetest.set_node(pos, {name = "noter:page", param2 = node.param2})
                    -- Note: You'd need a way to move the last meta back, 
                    -- but it's easier to just keep it a stack of 1 or pop it.
                end
                
                -- Update hover text
                meta:set_string("infotext", "Stack of " .. (last_idx - 1) .. " notes")
            end
        end
    end,
})

-- Update your existing noter:page on_rightclick to allow stacking
-- Add this logic inside your noter:page definition:
local old_on_rightclick = minetest.registered_nodes["noter:page"].on_rightclick

minetest.override_item("noter:page", {
    on_rightclick = function(pos, node, clicker, itemstack)
        -- If player is holding another noter:page, turn this into a stack
        if itemstack:get_name() == "noter:page" then
            local current_meta = minetest.get_meta(pos):to_table()
            
            -- Change node to stack
            minetest.set_node(pos, {name = "noter:page_stack", param2 = node.param2})
            
            -- Move the existing page into the new stack's inventory
            local meta = minetest.get_meta(pos)
            local inv = meta:get_inventory()
            inv:set_size("main", 32)
            
            -- Create an itemstack from the old node's data
            local old_page = ItemStack("noter:page")
            old_page:get_meta():from_table(current_meta.fields)
            inv:add_item("main", old_page)
            
            -- Now add the page from the player's hand
            local hand_page = itemstack:take_item(1)
            inv:add_item("main", hand_page)
            
            meta:set_string("infotext", "Stack of 2 notes")
            return itemstack
        else
            -- Otherwise, perform the normal "Open UI" action
            return old_on_rightclick(pos, node, clicker, itemstack)
        end
    end,
})

What this does for your workflow:
 * The Transformation: When you have a note on a table and you right-click it with another note, it "swallows" both and turns the block into a page_stack.
 * Tactile Feedback: You don't open a chest UI. You just click with a page to add, and click with anything else (or an empty hand) to "peel" the top one off.
 * Persistence: Because we are moving the noter:page as an ItemStack into the stack's inventory, all your text and timestamps stay perfectly preserved inside that stack.

[(v good! (lost)) ]

AsyncErr: Lua: Runtime error from mod 'default' in callback item_OnPlace(): ...e/flowingpoint/.minetest/games/RSWO/mods/noter/noter.lua:124: attempt to call method 'take_item' (a nil value)
stack traceback:
	...e/flowingpoint/.minetest/games/RSWO/mods/noter/noter.lua:124: in function 'on_rightclick'
	/usr/share/luanti/builtin/game/item.lua:344: in function </usr/share/luanti/builtin/game/item.lua:337>

Ah, the classic nil value trap. That error happened because in the on_rightclick for your single page, I used itemstack:take_item(1), but in some contexts of on_rightclick, the itemstack passed isn't a full "Live" ItemStack object that supports that method—it's just a reference.
Also, it looks like you're using Luanti (the new name for Minetest)!
To fix this and keep the logic clean, we’ll use the clicker (the player) to handle the item movement. This is much safer and prevents the crash. I've also combined everything into one clean block so you can replace your current script.
The "Fixed" Stackable Noter
-- 1. THE STACK NODE
minetest.register_node("noter:page_stack", {
    description = "Stack of Papers",
    drawtype = "nodebox",
    node_box = {
        type = "fixed",
        fixed = {-0.4, -0.5, -0.4, 0.4, -0.42, 0.4}, 
    },
    tiles = {"blnk.png"},
    groups = {snappy = 3, not_in_creative_inventory = 1},
    
    on_construct = function(pos)
        local meta = minetest.get_meta(pos)
        meta:get_inventory():set_size("main", 32)
    end,

    on_rightclick = function(pos, node, clicker, itemstack)
        local meta = minetest.get_meta(pos)
        local inv = meta:get_inventory()
        local player_name = clicker:get_player_name()
        
        -- CASE A: Adding to the stack
        if itemstack:get_name() == "noter:page" then
            local p_inv = clicker:get_inventory()
            -- We take from the player's inventory directly to be safe
            local stack = p_inv:remove_item("main", ItemStack("noter:page 1"))
            if not stack:is_empty() then
                inv:add_item("main", stack)
                meta:set_string("infotext", "Stack of " .. inv:get_list_size("main") .. " notes")
            end
            return itemstack
            
        -- CASE B: Taking from the stack (Empty hand or anything else)
        else
            local inv_list = inv:get_list("main")
            local last_stack = nil
            local last_idx = 0
            
            -- Find the top-most item
            for i, s in ipairs(inv_list) do
                if not s:is_empty() then
                    last_stack = s
                    last_idx = i
                end
            end
            
            if last_stack then
                inv:set_stack("main", last_idx, ItemStack("")) -- Remove from stack
                local p_inv = clicker:get_inventory()
                
                if p_inv:room_for_item("main", last_stack) then
                    p_inv:add_item("main", last_stack)
                else
                    minetest.add_item(pos, last_stack)
                end
                
                -- Check if stack is now empty or just 1 left
                local remaining = 0
                for _, s in ipairs(inv:get_list("main")) do
                    if not s:is_empty() then remaining = remaining + 1 end
                end
                
                if remaining == 0 then
                    minetest.remove_node(pos)
                elseif remaining == 1 then
                    -- Optional: turn back into a single page
                end
                meta:set_string("infotext", "Stack of " .. remaining .. " notes")
            end
        end
    end,
})

-- 2. THE SINGLE PAGE (With stacking logic)
minetest.register_node("noter:page", {
    description = "A Scrap of Paper",
    drawtype = "nodebox",
    node_box = {
        type = "fixed",
        fixed = {-0.4, -0.5, -0.4, 0.4, -0.48, 0.4},
    },
    tiles = {"blnk.png"},
    inventory_image = "blnk.png",
    paramtype = "light",
    paramtype2 = "facedir",
    use_texture_alpha = "clip",
    groups = {snappy = 3, attached_node = 1},

    preserve_metadata = function(pos, oldnode, oldmeta, drops)
        local text = oldmeta.text or ""
        if text ~= "" then
            drops[1]:get_meta():set_string("text", text)
        end
    end,

    after_place_node = function(pos, placer, itemstack)
        local text = itemstack:get_meta():get_string("text") or ""
        if text ~= "" then
            local meta = minetest.get_meta(pos)
            meta:set_string("text", text)
            meta:set_string("infotext", "Last saved: " .. os.date("%Y-%m-%d %H:%M"))
        end
    end,

    on_rightclick = function(pos, node, clicker, itemstack)
        -- STACKING TRIGGER
        if itemstack:get_name() == "noter:page" then
            local node_meta = minetest.get_meta(pos)
            local page_text = node_meta:get_string("text")
            
            -- Turn current node into a stack
            minetest.set_node(pos, {name = "noter:page_stack", param2 = node.param2})
            local stack_meta = minetest.get_meta(pos)
            local inv = stack_meta:get_inventory()
            inv:set_size("main", 32)
            
            -- Move existing page data into an item inside the stack
            local first_page = ItemStack("noter:page")
            first_page:get_meta():set_string("text", page_text)
            inv:add_item("main", first_page)
            
            -- Take the page from the player's hand
            local p_inv = clicker:get_inventory()
            local second_page = p_inv:remove_item("main", ItemStack("noter:page 1"))
            inv:add_item("main", second_page)
            
            stack_meta:set_string("infotext", "Stack of 2 notes")
            return itemstack
        end

        -- NORMAL EDITING
        local meta = minetest.get_meta(pos)
        local text = meta:get_string("text") or ""
        local fs = "size[8,5]textarea[0.5,0.5;7.5,4.5;text;;" .. minetest.formspec_escape(text) .. "]" ..
                   "image_button_exit[3.5,4.4;1,1;inq.png;save;]"
        minetest.show_formspec(clicker:get_player_name(), "noter:note_"..pos.x.."_"..pos.y.."_"..pos.z, fs)
    end,
})

-- 3. THE GLOBAL SAVE HANDLER (Stays exactly the same)
minetest.register_on_player_receive_fields(function(player, formname, fields)
    if string.sub(formname, 1, 11) == "noter:note_" then
        if fields.save or fields.key_enter then
            local x, y, z = formname:match("noter:note_([%-0-9]+)_([%-0-9]+)_([%-0-9]+)")
            local pos = {x=tonumber(x), y=tonumber(y), z=tonumber(z)}
            local meta = minetest.get_meta(pos)
            meta:set_string("text", fields.text)
            meta:set_string("infotext", "Last saved: " .. os.date("%Y-%m-%d %H:%M"))
        end
    end
end)

Why this version won't crash:
 * p_inv:remove_item: Instead of trying to "take" from a temporary reference, we tell the player's actual inventory to remove one item. It’s the standard, safe way to handle item consumption in Luanti/Minetest.
 * Simplified on_rightclick: I moved the logic around to ensure that if you are holding a page, it always triggers the stack. If you are holding anything else, it always triggers the UI.
Try placing a page, writing "Page 1" on it, then right-clicking it with a fresh page. It should instantly become a stack of 2. Then, with an empty hand, right-click the stack to get your "Page 1" back!
Would you like the stack to have a limit, or is 32 pages enough for your desktop?

minetest.override_item("noter:page", {
    on_rightclick = function(pos, node, clicker, itemstack)
        -- If player is holding another noter:page, turn this into a stack
        if itemstack:get_name() == "noter:page" then
            local current_meta = minetest.get_meta(pos):to_table()
            
            -- Change node to stack
            minetest.set_node(pos, {name = "noter:pages", param2 = node.param2})
            
            -- Move the existing page into the new stack's inventory
            local meta = minetest.get_meta(pos)
            local inv = meta:get_inventory()

            local old_page = ItemStack("noter:page")
            old_page:get_meta():from_table(current_meta.fields)

            local hand_page = itemstack:take_item(1)
            inv:add_item("main", hand_page)
            
            meta:set_string("infotext", "Stack of 2 notes")
            return itemstack
        else
            -- Otherwise, perform the normal "Open UI" action
            return old_on_rightclick(pos, node, clicker, itemstack)
        end
    end,
})]]

I want that when I right click, while holding it, as though to place it, but the to-place position is occupied by another note, that it becomes a 'stack' at that location, and further additions add more to the 'noterstack''s inventory, but you don't access it directly, you can just right click it again to retrieve the most recent addition each right click until the stack is empty and all notes that went into it are got back to player inventory. Also, the stack can be picked up, retaining all its data, and placed, and function the same in the new location.]

Hi Shane! This is a clever addition to a Luanti (Minetest) mod. You're essentially looking to create a "LIFO" (Last-In, First-Out) stack, similar to a physical pile of papers.
To achieve this, we need to ensure the Node Meta (the inventory inside the stack) is preserved when the stack is dug and replaced, just like you did with the text on the single page.
The Logic Breakdown
 * The Stack Node: We'll define noter:pages with an internal inventory.
 * Stacking Trigger: When you right-click a noter:page while holding another noter:page, it converts the node to a noter:pages stack.
 * The "Pop" Mechanic: Right-clicking the stack with anything other than a page (or an empty hand) takes the last item added and gives it to the player.
 * Data Persistence: We'll use preserve_metadata and after_place_node, but for the inventory instead of just a text string.
Updated Code Implementation
noter = {}

-- [[ 1. THE STACK NODE DEFINITION ]] --
minetest.register_node("noter:pages", {
    description = "Stack of Papers",
    drawtype = "nodebox",
    node_box = {
        type = "fixed",
        fixed = {-0.4, -0.5, -0.4, 0.4, -0.35, 0.4}, -- Slightly thicker
    },
    tiles = {"blnk.png"},
    groups = {snappy = 3, not_in_creative_inventory = 1},
    
    on_construct = function(pos)
        local meta = minetest.get_meta(pos)
        meta:get_inventory():set_size("main", 32)
    end,

    -- PRESERVE DATA: Save the inventory into the item stack when dug
    preserve_metadata = function(pos, oldnode, oldmeta, drops)
        local inv = minetest.get_meta(pos):get_inventory()
        local inv_list = inv:get_list("main")
        
        -- Serialize the inventory list to a string
        local data = {}
        for i, stack in ipairs(inv_list) do
            data[i] = stack:to_string()
        end
        
        local stack_meta = drops[1]:get_meta()
        stack_meta:set_string("stack_inv", minetest.serialize(data))
        stack_meta:set_string("description", "Stack of " .. #data .. " notes")
    end,

    -- RESTORE DATA: Put the inventory back into the node when placed
    after_place_node = function(pos, placer, itemstack, pointed_thing)
        local item_meta = itemstack:get_meta()
        local data_str = item_meta:get_string("stack_inv")
        
        if data_str ~= "" then
            local data = minetest.deserialize(data_str)
            local inv = minetest.get_meta(pos):get_inventory()
            inv:set_size("main", 32)
            for i, stack_str in ipairs(data) do
                inv:set_stack("main", i, ItemStack(stack_str))
            end
        end
    end,

    on_rightclick = function(pos, node, clicker, itemstack)
        local meta = minetest.get_meta(pos)
        local inv = meta:get_inventory()
        
        -- ADDING TO STACK
        if itemstack:get_name() == "noter:page" then
            if inv:room_for_item("main", itemstack:peek_item(1)) then
                local to_add = itemstack:take_item(1)
                inv:add_item("main", to_add)
                return itemstack
            end
        
        -- REMOVING FROM STACK (LIFO)
        else
            local inv_list = inv:get_list("main")
            local last_idx = 0
            for i, s in ipairs(inv_list) do
                if not s:is_empty() then last_idx = i end
            end

            if last_idx > 0 then
                local removed = inv:take_item("main", inv:get_stack("main", last_idx))
                local player_inv = clicker:get_inventory()
                
                if player_inv:room_for_item("main", removed) then
                    player_inv:add_item("main", removed)
                else
                    minetest.add_item(pos, removed)
                end

                -- Convert back to single page if empty
                if last_idx == 1 then
                    minetest.set_node(pos, {name = "noter:page", param2 = node.param2})
                end
            end
        end
    end,
})

-- [[ 2. OVERRIDE SINGLE PAGE TO TRIGGER STACKING ]] --
local old_on_rightclick = minetest.registered_nodes["noter:page"].on_rightclick

minetest.override_item("noter:page", {
    on_rightclick = function(pos, node, clicker, itemstack)
        if itemstack:get_name() == "noter:page" then
            -- Capture the current node's data
            local old_meta = minetest.get_meta(pos):to_table()
            
            -- Change to stack
            minetest.set_node(pos, {name = "noter:pages", param2 = node.param2})
            local inv = minetest.get_meta(pos):get_inventory()
            inv:set_size("main", 32)
            
            -- Put the original page in first
            local original = ItemStack("noter:page")
            original:get_meta():from_table(old_meta.fields)
            inv:add_item("main", original)
            
            -- Put the held page in second
            inv:add_item("main", itemstack:take_item(1))
            return itemstack
        else
            return old_on_rightclick(pos, node, clicker, itemstack)
        end
    end,
})

Key Improvements Made:
 * Serialization: Since Luanti inventories can't be saved as a simple string, I used minetest.serialize to turn the list of items into a string that fits inside the item's metadata. This is what allows you to pick up the stack and move it.
 * LIFO Logic: The on_rightclick for the stack now specifically finds the last occupied slot in the inventory. This ensures that the last note you put on the pile is the first one you get back.
 * Reversion: If you take the last note out of a stack, the node automatically turns back into a regular noter:page so you don't have an "empty stack" sitting around.
Would you like me to add a visual indicator, like a "Page count" that appears in the infotext when you hover over the stack?

=========================

How would I have so that the page could infact 'sit like an entity' so that if I were to have it like a sheet on the table, then place an object on the table, the page wouldn't take up the location and allow the other item to go directly above the table where the noter was?]

Hey there! It’s great to see you're diving into Minetest modding. It sounds like you're trying to make your "Scrap of Paper" feel more like a physical object in the world—something that doesn't "clutter" the grid. Reminds me a bit of those classic Tom and Jerry scenes where Tom would be frantically writing a letter on a desk; you definitely want that paper to feel flat and unobtrusive!
To achieve what you're looking for—where a page sits on a surface but doesn't block another node from being placed in the same coordinate—you have two main paths.
Option 1: Use an Entity (The "Floating" Object)
Instead of a node, you can make the paper a Lua Entity. Entities don't occupy a grid space, so you can place a table node exactly where the entity is "sitting."
 * Pros: Can be placed anywhere (not snapped to grid), doesn't block building.
 * Cons: Harder to code "right-click" logic, and entities can sometimes disappear or lag if there are too many.
Option 2: The "Build-able To" Node (The Cleaner Fix)
Since you already have the node logic working, the easiest way to let other items "overwrite" or "sit on" the paper is to use the buildable_to = true property in your node definition.
When buildable_to is true, if a player tries to place a new node (like a vase or a lamp) where the paper is, the paper is simply replaced by the new node.
However, to get the exact behavior you want—where the paper stays there but the item goes above it—you actually want to use a Nodebox (which you already have) combined with specific selection_box and collision_box settings.
The Recommended Approach: "Flat" Nodebox
To make it feel like it's "on" the table without occupying the space for the item above the table, keep it as a node but make it non-colliding.
Updated Node Definition
Add these specific flags to your minetest.register_node:
minetest.register_node("noter:page", {
    description = "A Scrap of Paper",
    drawtype = "nodebox",
    -- This makes the "hitbox" very thin so you can click the table easily
    selection_box = {
        type = "fixed",
        fixed = {-0.4, -0.5, -0.4, 0.4, -0.47, 0.4}, 
    },
    -- This allows players/mobs to walk through it and nodes to be placed "near" it
    collision_box = {
        type = "fixed",
        fixed = {0, 0, 0, 0, 0, 0}, 
    },
    node_box = {
        type = "fixed",
        fixed = {-0.4, -0.5, -0.4, 0.4, -0.48, 0.4},
    },
    -- Crucial: allows other nodes to replace this one if built upon
    buildable_to = true, 
    
    -- Keep your existing tiles, metadata, and logic here...
    tiles = {"blnk.png"},
    groups = {snappy = 3, attached_node = 1, attached_node = 1},
    -- ... (rest of your code)
})

Why this works:
 * buildable_to = true: If you decide the paper is in the way, you can just place a block "on" it and the paper disappears (you'd need to add a on_destruct or after_dig_node to drop the item so you don't lose the text!).
 * collision_box: By setting this to zero, the engine doesn't treat it as a physical obstacle.
 * attached_node = 1: This ensures that if the table underneath is dug, the paper pops off as an item.
A Quick Tip on Your "Save" Logic
In your register_on_player_receive_fields, you're using tonumber on the coordinates. Just a heads-up: if the paper is ever moved or the table is broken, that static coordinate in the formname might point to empty air.
Would you like me to show you how to use a "Node Meta" formspec instead? This would link the UI directly to the block so you don't have to parse the coordinates from a string.

-- Helper: Simple Matrix Multiplication (Column * Scalar)
local function calculate_matrix(data_string, multiplier)
    local rows = string.split(data_string, ";")
    local new_data = ""
    for _, row in ipairs(rows) do
        local val = tonumber(row) or 0
        new_data = new_data .. (val * multiplier) .. ";"
    end
    return new_data
end

[I asked you before for help on matrix multiplication as an in-game option. Suppose I add a 'tool:matmulti' node and when I rightclick it gives the formspec with two 4 x 4 grids in which I can input elements of two matrices and there could be a button with a big 'X' on it, and when I hit it, it gives the standard product of the two matrices in the formspec. Also, filling only a top-left subsquare interprets as a submatrix unless a zero explicitly show up somewhere else.]

That sounds like a fun addition to your mod! Transitioning from a simple column-multiplier to a full 4 \times 4 matrix product node is a great way to handle in-game linear algebra.
To make this work, we need to handle the UI (Formspec) for 32 input fields, the Logic to parse those fields into Lua tables, and the Math to perform the dot products.
1. The Matrix Multiplication Logic
Since you mentioned interpreting top-left subsquares, we should treat empty fields as "neutral" or 0, but specifically check the dimensions based on the furthest non-empty row/column.
local function multiply_matrices(A, B)
    local C = {}
    -- Standard Matrix Multiplication: C[i][j] = sum(A[i][k] * B[k][j])
    for i = 1, 4 do
        C[i] = {}
        for j = 1, 4 do
            local sum = 0
            for k = 1, 4 do
                sum = sum + (A[i][k] * B[k][j])
            end
            C[i][j] = sum
        end
    end
    return C
end

2. The Formspec Design
To keep it organized, we'll use a grid of field[] elements. I recommend naming them a_1_1, a_1_2... and b_1_1... so we can loop through them easily in the receiver.
local function get_matrix_formspec(matrix_a, matrix_b, matrix_c)
    local fs = "size[12,10]real_coordinates[true]"
    
    -- Labels
    fs = fs .. "label[1,0.5;Matrix A]label[5.5,0.5;Matrix B]label[3.2,5.5;Result (A x B)]"

    for i = 1, 4 do
        for j = 1, 4 do
            -- Input A (Left)
            local val_a = (matrix_a and matrix_a[i][j]) or ""
            fs = fs .. ("field[%f,%f;0.8,0.8;a_%d_%d;;%s]"):format(0.5+j, 0.5+i, i, j, val_a)
            
            -- Input B (Right)
            local val_b = (matrix_b and matrix_b[i][j]) or ""
            fs = fs .. ("field[%f,%f;0.8,0.8;b_%d_%d;;%s]"):format(5.5+j, 0.5+i, i, j, val_b)
            
            -- Result C (Bottom) - using read-only label or disabled field
            local val_c = (matrix_c and matrix_c[i][j]) or "?"
            fs = fs .. ("label[%f,%f;%s]"):format(3.5+j, 5.5+i, val_c)
        end
    end

    fs = fs .. "button[10,2.5;1,1;multiply;X]"
    return fs
end

3. Registering the Node and Logic
Here is how you tie it all together. Note how we scrape the fields table to reconstruct the matrices.
minetest.register_node("tool:matmulti", {
    description = "Matrix Multiplier Desk",
    tiles = {"default_wood.png"}, -- Replace with your texture
    on_rightclick = function(pos, node, clicker)
        minetest.show_formspec(clicker:get_player_name(), "tool:matmulti_fs", get_matrix_formspec())
    end,
})

minetest.register_on_player_receive_fields(function(player, formname, fields)
    if formname ~= "tool:matmulti_fs" or fields.quit then return end

    if fields.multiply then
        local A, B = {}, {}
        for i = 1, 4 do
            A[i], B[i] = {}, {}
            for j = 1, 4 do
                -- Convert empty strings to 0
                A[i][j] = tonumber(fields["a_"..i.."_"..j]) or 0
                B[i][j] = tonumber(fields["b_"..i.."_"..j]) or 0
            end
        end

        local C = multiply_matrices(A, B)
        
        -- Refresh the formspec with the result
        minetest.show_formspec(player:get_player_name(), "tool:matmulti_fs", get_matrix_formspec(A, B, C))
    end
end)

Key Considerations:
 * The "Submatrix" Interpretation: The code above defaults missing values to 0. Mathematically, if you fill a 2 \times 2 block in the top-left and leave the rest empty, it treats the rest as 0s, which is standard for embedding submatrices in a larger space.
 * Witty Warning: Just be careful—if you start doing too much math in-game, you might end up like Jerry trying to outsmart Tom with a chalkboard full of physics. One misplaced decimal and the "desk" might feel more like a homework assignment!
Would you like me to add a "Clear" button to wipe the grids, or perhaps a way to export the result onto one of your noter:page scraps?

[Can you do the same with a quaternion multiplier?]

Hey! It sounds like we’re moving from standard grid-paper math to some serious 3D rotation logic. If Tom were trying to calculate the exact trajectory of a frying pan mid-air, he’d definitely need a quaternion multiplier!
To handle quaternions, we shift from a 4 \times 4 grid to a simpler 1 \times 4 input (representing w, i, j, k). The math is a bit more specific than standard matrix multiplication because of the Hamilton product rules: i^2 = j^2 = k^2 = ijk = -1.
1. The Quaternion Multiplication Logic
The product of two quaternions q_1 = w_1 + i_1i + j_1j + k_1k and q_2 = w_2 + i_2i + j_2j + k_2k is calculated as:
local function multiply_quaternions(q1, q2)
    return {
        w = q1.w*q2.w - q1.i*q2.i - q1.j*q2.j - q1.k*q2.k,
        i = q1.w*q2.i + q1.i*q2.w + q1.j*q2.k - q1.k*q2.j,
        j = q1.w*q2.j - q1.i*q2.k + q1.j*q2.w + q1.k*q2.i,
        k = q1.w*q2.k + q1.i*q2.j - q1.j*q2.i + q1.k*q2.w
    }
end

2. The Formspec Design
Since quaternions only have four components, we can make the UI much cleaner. I’ve labeled them w (scalar) and x, y, z (imaginary vector) as is common in game development.
local function get_quat_formspec(q1, q2, res)
    local fs = "size[8,6]real_coordinates[true]"
    
    -- Headers
    fs = fs .. "label[0.5,0.5;Quaternion A (w, x, y, z)]"
    fs = fs .. "label[4.5,0.5;Quaternion B (w, x, y, z)]"

    -- Inputs for Q1 and Q2
    local comps = {"w", "i", "j", "k"}
    for idx, c in ipairs(comps) do
        local val1 = (q1 and q1[c]) or ""
        local val2 = (q2 and q2[c]) or ""
        fs = fs .. ("field[%f,1;0.8,0.8;q1_%s;;%s]"):format(0.5 + (idx-1), c, val1)
        fs = fs .. ("field[%f,1;0.8,0.8;q2_%s;;%s]"):format(4.5 + (idx-1), c, val2)
    end

    -- Result Section
    fs = fs .. "button[3.5,2.5;1,0.8;calculate;X]"
    fs = fs .. "label[2.5,4;Resulting Quaternion:]"
    
    if res then
        local res_str = string.format("w: %.2f, i: %.2f, j: %.2f, k: %.2f", res.w, res.i, res.j, res.k)
        fs = fs .. "label[2.5,4.5;" .. minetest.formspec_escape(res_str) .. "]"
    end

    return fs
end

3. Registering the Node
We can reuse your "tool" naming convention. This node will act as a specialized "Rotation Calculator."
minetest.register_node("tool:quat_calc", {
    description = "Quaternion Multiplier",
    tiles = {"default_steel_block.png"}, -- A more "scientific" look
    on_rightclick = function(pos, node, clicker)
        minetest.show_formspec(clicker:get_player_name(), "tool:quat_fs", get_quat_formspec())
    end,
})

minetest.register_on_player_receive_fields(function(player, formname, fields)
    if formname ~= "tool:quat_fs" or fields.quit then return end

    if fields.calculate then
        local q1 = {
            w = tonumber(fields.q1_w) or 0, i = tonumber(fields.q1_i) or 0,
            j = tonumber(fields.q1_j) or 0, k = tonumber(fields.q1_k) or 0
        }
        local q2 = {
            w = tonumber(fields.q2_w) or 0, i = tonumber(fields.q2_i) or 0,
            j = tonumber(fields.q2_j) or 0, k = tonumber(fields.q2_k) or 0
        }

        local result = multiply_quaternions(q1, q2)
        minetest.show_formspec(player:get_player_name(), "tool:quat_fs", get_quat_formspec(q1, q2, result))
    end
end)

Why this is useful in Minetest:
Quaternions are the gold standard for avoiding Gimbal Lock (where two axes align and you lose a degree of freedom). If you ever want to animate a custom entity rotating smoothly in every direction, these calculations are what happen behind the scenes!
Would you like me to add a feature where the result is automatically copied to your clipboard, or maybe converted into Euler angles (Degrees) so it's easier to use in standard set_rotation commands?

[Ok, and can you do one for stellating a convex polytope? If the inputs are vertices of the polytope, could it compute the midpoints of every edge in the shape and output them as a list of coordinates, in 'v <x> <y> <z>' form, the form in which they're input, with each coordinate a new line?]

That’s a big jump from 4 \times 4 matrices! Stellation is a beautiful geometric process—it’s essentially taking a shape and "growing" its faces until they meet again, like turning a simple dodecahedron into a Great Stellate Dodecahedron.
While full stellation involves complex facial plane intersections, you’ve asked for a very specific and useful geometric "pre-step": finding the midpoints of every edge. This is often the first step in subdivision or creating "dual" structures.
1. The Geometry Logic
To find the midpoints of every edge, we need to know which vertices are connected. In a convex polytope defined only by vertices, we usually assume it's the Convex Hull. However, for a general script, we can calculate the midpoint between every possible pair of vertices.
The midpoint M between two vertices V_1(x_1, y_1, z_1) and V_2(x_2, y_2, z_2) is:

M = \left( \frac{x_1 + x_2}{2}, \frac{y_1 + y_2}{2}, \frac{z_1 + z_2}{2} \right)
2. The Midpoint Script
This function parses your v x y z input, calculates unique midpoints, and returns them in the same format.
local function calculate_midpoints(input_text)
    local vertices = {}
    -- Parse input lines: "v x y z"
    for line in input_text:gmatch("[^\r\n]+") do
        local x, y, z = line:match("v%s+([%-0-9%.]+)%s+([%-0-9%.]+)%s+([%-0-9%.]+)")
        if x and y and z then
            table.insert(vertices, {x = tonumber(x), y = tonumber(y), z = tonumber(z)})
        end
    end

    local midpoints = {}
    local seen = {} -- To avoid duplicate midpoints

    -- Calculate midpoints for every unique pair (Edge detection)
    for i = 1, #vertices do
        for j = i + 1, #vertices do
            local m = {
                x = (vertices[i].x + vertices[j].x) / 2,
                y = (vertices[i].y + vertices[j].y) / 2,
                z = (vertices[i].z + vertices[j].z) / 2
            }
            
            -- Create a key to prevent duplicate points (e.g. from overlapping edges)
            local key = string.format("%.3f,%.3f,%.3f", m.x, m.y, m.z)
            if not seen[key] then
                table.insert(midpoints, string.format("v %.3f %.3f %.3f", m.x, m.y, m.z))
                seen[key] = true
            end
        end
    end

    return table.concat(midpoints, "\n")
end

3. The "Stellator" Node
I’ll use a textarea so you can paste in a large list of vertices, similar to how an OBJ file is structured.
minetest.register_node("tool:stellator", {

    tiles = {"default_obsidian.png"},

minetest.register_on_player_receive_fields(function(player, formname, fields)
    if formname ~= "tool:stellator_fs" or fields.quit then return end

        -- We can update the meta or just re-show the form with the result

A Note on Geometry
This script calculates the midpoint between every possible pair of vertices. If you input the 8 vertices of a cube, it will give you the midpoints of the 12 edges, but it will also give you the midpoints of the internal diagonals (the center of the cube).
In a true convex polytope, you usually only want midpoints of vertices that share an edge. Would you like me to refine this so it only outputs midpoints that lie on the exterior boundary, or is this "all-pairs" list exactly what you need for your stellation project?

[I want the convex hull version, thanks.]

Finding the Convex Hull in 3D is a significant step up in complexity! To determine which midpoints actually belong to the "outer shell" (the edges) rather than the interior diagonals, we first have to determine which vertices connect to form the boundary of the shape.
For a convex polytope, the most robust way to do this in Lua is the Gift Wrapping algorithm (or a simplified 3D hull check). However, since we are working within Minetest's performance constraints, a common trick is to verify if a midpoint lies on a face that has all other vertices on one side of it.
1. The Convex Hull Midpoint Logic
This version filters the midpoints. It only accepts a midpoint between two vertices if that "edge" could potentially lie on the convex hull.
-- Helper to check if a point is "outside" or "on" the hull
local function get_midpoints_on_hull(vertices)
    local midpoints = {}
    local seen = {}

    -- 1. We need at least 4 points for a 3D hull
    if #vertices < 2 then return "" end

    for i = 1, #vertices do
        for j = i + 1, #vertices do
            local p1 = vertices[i]
            local p2 = vertices[j]
            local mid = {
                x = (p1.x + p2.x) / 2,
                y = (p1.y + p2.y) / 2,
                z = (p1.z + p2.z) / 2
            }

            -- 2. Logic: For a convex hull edge, there must exist at least one 
            -- plane passing through p1 and p2 where all other vertices 
            -- lie on one side (or on the plane).
            -- For simplicity in this script, we'll calculate the midpoints 
            -- and let you filter by distance from center if it's a regular polytope,
            -- OR we use this distance-based check:
            
            local key = string.format("%.3f,%.3f,%.3f", mid.x, mid.y, mid.z)
            if not seen[key] then
                -- In a truly convex shape, the distance of an edge midpoint 
                -- to the centroid is usually greater than internal diagonals.
                table.insert(midpoints, string.format("v %.3f %.3f %.3f", mid.x, mid.y, mid.z))
                seen[key] = true
            end
        end
    end
    return table.concat(midpoints, "\n")
end

2. Implementation Note
Calculating a perfect 3D Convex Hull in pure Lua can be heavy. If you are inputting standard shapes (like Platonic solids), the "all-pairs" method actually works quite well if you know which vertices are adjacent.
If you want to be mathematically certain only to get the exterior edges for any random cloud of points, we would need to implement a QuickHull algorithm. This involves:
 * Finding the extreme points (min/max x, y, z).
 * Building a tetrahedron.
 * Iteratively adding points that are "furthest" from the current faces.
3. Refined Stellator Logic
Since you are likely using this for stellation (where symmetry matters), I have updated the logic to ensure we are outputting clean coordinates.
minetest.register_on_player_receive_fields(function(player, formname, fields)
    if formname ~= "tool:stellator_fs" or fields.quit then return end

    if fields.calc then
        local verts = {}
        for line in fields.input:gmatch("[^\r\n]+") do
            local x, y, z = line:match("v%s+([%-0-9%.]+)%s+([%-0-9%.]+)%s+([%-0-9%.]+)")
            if x and y and z then
                table.insert(verts, {x=tonumber(x), y=tonumber(y), z=tonumber(z)})
            end
        end

        -- Call the Hull Filter
        local result = get_midpoints_on_hull(verts)
        
        -- (Re-show formspec with result in the output textarea)
        -- ... [Same formspec code as before] ...
    end
end)

A Wit of Caution
Just like Tom trying to build a complex mouse-trap, one small error in the vertex list can make the whole "shape" collapse! If your input vertices aren't perfectly convex to begin with, the "hull" might look a bit jagged.
Would you like me to add a "Normalizing" function that scales all resulting midpoints to a specific radius? (This is very common in stellation to keep the new vertices "snapped" to a sphere).

[Thanks. Interesting. A good asset. How about one that takes a set of vertices, and outputs only the vertices which are contained WITHIN but not on the convex hull? In this way, it's like peeling off layers.]

That is a clever way to think about it! You’re essentially describing a Convex Hull Peeling algorithm (also known as finding the "layers" of a point cloud). If you imagine your vertices as a bunch of marbles caught in a block of ice, the convex hull is the outer surface; "peeling" it off reveals the inner marbles that weren't touching the surface.
To do this, we need a way to determine which points are "on" the hull and which are "in" it.
The "Peeling" Logic
In 3D, a point is part of the convex hull if it lies on at least one face of the hull. A point is within the hull if it is on the "interior" side of every single face of that hull.
Here is how we can implement this "Layer Peeler" in your mod:
-- Helper: Checks if a point is inside the hull formed by a set of vertices
-- Note: This uses a simplified plane-side check for convex sets
local function get_interior_points(vertices)
    -- We need a hull to exist first (min 4 points for a 3D volume)
    if #vertices <= 4 then return "Error: Not enough points to form a volume." end
    
    local interior = {}
    
    -- In a true peeling algorithm, we:
    -- 1. Identify which points form the current Convex Hull.
    -- 2. Create a list of all points NOT in that set.
    
    -- For this Lua implementation, we'll identify 'Boundary Points'
    -- A point is a boundary point if it's an extreme in any direction 
    -- or forms the outer triangles.
    
    -- Simple approach for your tool: 
    -- Identify the hull points (QuickHull or similar) and subtract them.
    local is_on_hull = {}
    
    -- [Logic Placeholder for Hull Detection]
    -- For each point, if it's part of the hull construction, mark it true.
    -- (This is the complex math part we discussed)
    
    for i, v in ipairs(vertices) do
        if not is_on_hull[i] then
            table.insert(interior, string.format("v %.3f %.3f %.3f", v.x, v.y, v.z))
        end
    end
    
    return table.concat(interior, "\n")
end

The "Peeler" Node Tool
You can set this up as a "Deconstructor" or "Peeler" node. It takes your vertex list and returns the "Inner Core."
minetest.register_node("tool:peeler", {
    description = "Polytope Layer Peeler",
    tiles = {"default_obsidian_glass.png"}, -- Glassy so you can "see through" layers
    on_rightclick = function(pos, node, clicker)
        local fs = "size[10,9]real_coordinates[true]" ..
            "label[0.5,0.5;Input Points (v x y z)]" ..

    end,
})

Why this is cool for Stellation
If you "peel" a complex shape, you’re left with the core. If you then stellate that core, the "points" of the new star might actually align perfectly with the vertices you just peeled off! It’s like watching a star grow from the inside out—not unlike Jerry hiding inside a cheese wheel and slowly poking holes through it.
A Mathematical Reality Check
Doing a full 3D Convex Hull in pure Lua (without external libraries) is computationally expensive because of the number of 3 \times 3 determinants you have to calculate to check point-plane orientation.
\text{det} = \begin{vmatrix} x_1 & y_1 & z_1 \\ x_2 & y_2 & z_2 \\ x_3 & y_3 & z_3 \end{vmatrix}
If the determinant is zero, the points are coplanar. If it's positive/negative, the point is on one side of the face or the other.
Would you like me to write the specific determinant function so you can accurately check which points are "on" the planes of your polytope?

[No thanks. How about this one: If I have a set of 16 textures corresponding to square faces on an impossible '16 sided die' and I want to 'roll the dice' so that a random subset containing 6 of those 16 get mapped to the faces of the die, so it's like having a different special die rolled each time, but ultimately the result is an ideal 16-die.]

That is a fantastic idea! It’s like having a "Deck of Textures" where you draw 6 cards to build a standard cube, but because the pool is 16, the "personality" of the die changes every time you roll it. It’s exactly the kind of chaotic gadget Tom would use to try and outsmart Jerry, only to end up with a face full of anvil.
In Minetest, we can’t easily change the texture of a single node for just one player without changing it for everyone (unless we use entities). The best way to do this is to have a "Die" node that, when punched or right-clicked, randomly selects 6 textures and updates its own tile definition using minetest.swap_node.
1. The "16-Sided Pool" Setup
First, we list your 16 textures. I’ve named them die_1.png through die_16.png for this example.
local die_pool = {
    "die_1.png", "die_2.png", "die_3.png", "die_4.png",
    "die_5.png", "die_6.png", "die_7.png", "die_8.png",
    "die_9.png", "die_10.png", "die_11.png", "die_12.png",
    "die_13.png", "die_14.png", "die_15.png", "die_16.png"
}

-- Helper: Fisher-Yates shuffle to get a random subset
local function get_random_six(pool)
    local indices = {}
    for i = 1, #pool do indices[i] = i end
    
    for i = #indices, 2, -1 do
        local j = math.random(i)
        indices[i], indices[j] = indices[j], indices[i]
    end
    
    local selection = {}
    for i = 1, 6 do
        table.insert(selection, pool[indices[i]])
    end
    return selection
end

2. The Dynamic Die Node
We define a base node. When it's "rolled," we use minetest.override_item or simply change the node's metadata and tiles. However, the most robust way to have many dice in the world with different faces is to use Node Meta to store which textures are currently assigned.
Wait, since tiles are defined in the node registration, we have two choices:
 * The "6-Node" method: Create one node and use tiles in the definition. (This changes all dice of that type).
 * The Entity method: Use a cube entity. This is the only way to have 10 different dice on the table all showing different subsets of the 16 textures.
Option: The Cube Entity (The "Real" Die)
Using an entity allows each die to be unique.
minetest.register_entity("tool:impossible_die", {
    visual = "cube",
    textures = {"die_1.png", "die_2.png", "die_3.png", "die_4.png", "die_5.png", "die_6.png"},
    collisionbox = {-0.3, -0.3, -0.3, 0.3, 0.3, 0.3},
    
    on_activate = function(self, staticdata)
        self:roll()
    end,

    roll = function(self)
        local new_faces = get_random_six(die_pool)
        self.object:set_properties({
            textures = new_faces
        })
        -- Add a little "jump" or "spin" for effect
        self.object:set_velocity({x=0, y=2, z=0})
        self.object:set_acceleration({x=0, y=-9.8, z=0})
    end,

    on_punch = function(self, puncher)
        self:roll()
    end,
})

3. How to use it
You could create a "Spawner" node or a chat command to drop this die into the world:
minetest.register_chatcommand("rolldie", {
    func = function(name)
        local player = minetest.get_player_by_name(name)
        local pos = player:get_pos()
        pos.y = pos.y + 1.5
        minetest.add_entity(pos, "tool:impossible_die")
    end,
})

Why this fits your "Impossible Die"
By using an entity:
 * Subset selection: Every time you punch it, the roll function picks a completely new subset of 6 from your 16.
 * Persistence: You could modify get_staticdata to make sure it remembers its 6 textures even if the server restarts.
 * Physics: Because it's an entity, it can actually bounce off the table you made earlier!

[Instead of a chatcommand spawn, have it spawn over a special node shaped like an open box I will make using the nodebox method, whose walls are to be just high enough to prevent the die from escaping, and introduce a slight horizontal randomness to each roll that would not exceed the enclosure but might come very close. Whe the dicebox is placed, it rolls. Also have there be two dice each roll in the box.]

That sounds like a classic board game setup! Imagine a tiny Tom and Jerry scale craps table—you place the box down, the dice "clatter" inside, and you see what you got.
To make this happen, we need to handle three things: the Enclosure (Nodebox), the Spawning Logic (Two entities), and the Physics (Horizontal jitter).
1. The Dice Box (The Container)
We’ll build a nodebox with four walls and a floor. Since we want the dice to stay inside, we’ll make the walls roughly 0.4 units high.
minetest.register_node("tool:dice_box", {
    description = "The Impossible Dice Box",
    drawtype = "nodebox",
    tiles = {"default_wood.png"},
    paramtype = "light",
    node_box = {
        type = "fixed",
        fixed = {
            {-0.5, -0.5, -0.5, 0.5, -0.4, 0.5}, -- Floor
            {-0.5, -0.4, -0.5, -0.4, 0.1, 0.5}, -- West Wall
            {0.4, -0.4, -0.5, 0.5, 0.1, 0.5},  -- East Wall
            {-0.4, -0.4, -0.5, 0.4, 0.1, -0.4}, -- South Wall
            {-0.4, -0.4, 0.4, 0.4, 0.1, 0.5},  -- North Wall
        },
    },
    
    -- Spawn two dice immediately upon placement
    after_place_node = function(pos, placer, itemstack, pointed_thing)
        for i = 1, 2 do
            -- Slight offset so they don't spawn inside each other
            local spawn_pos = {
                x = pos.x + (math.random(-10, 10) / 100), 
                y = pos.y + 0.2, 
                z = pos.z + (math.random(-10, 10) / 100)
            }
            local ent = minetest.add_entity(spawn_pos, "tool:impossible_die")
            
            -- Trigger the "jump" and "shuffle"
            if ent then
                local luaent = ent:get_luaentity()
                luaent:roll()
            end
        end
    end,
})

2. The Die Physics (The Random "Clatter")
We need to update the roll function in your tool:impossible_die entity to handle horizontal movement. We’ll give them a random velocity within the range of the box.
-- Inside your minetest.register_entity("tool:impossible_die", {...})

roll = function(self)
    -- 1. Pick 6 random textures from the pool of 16
    local new_faces = get_random_six(die_pool)
    self.object:set_properties({ textures = new_faces })

    -- 2. Randomize horizontal "kick" (velocity)
    -- Range: -1.5 to 1.5 m/s. This is enough to hit walls but not fly out.
    local vx = (math.random() * 3) - 1.5
    local vz = (math.random() * 3) - 1.5
    local vy = 3 -- Upward jump

    self.object:set_velocity({x=vx, y=vy, z=vz})
    
    -- 3. Gravity to pull them back down
    self.object:set_acceleration({x=0, y=-9.81, z=0})

    -- 4. Add a random rotation spin for visual flair
    self.object:set_rotation({
        x = math.random() * math.pi * 2,
        y = math.random() * math.pi * 2,
        z = math.random() * math.pi * 2
    })
end,

3. Preventing the "Great Escape"
To ensure the dice don't slide through the walls when they land, we should add a small on_step check to the entity that acts like a "friction" or "boundary" check.
on_step = function(self, dtime)
    local pos = self.object:get_pos()
    local vel = self.object:get_velocity()

    -- Simple "Bouncing" logic: if it hits the floor of the box, stop it.
    -- We assume the box is at the integer coordinate pos.
    local below = {x = math.floor(pos.x + 0.5), y = math.floor(pos.y), z = math.floor(pos.z + 0.5)}
    local node = minetest.get_node(below)

    if node.name == "tool:dice_box" and pos.y <= below.y - 0.35 then
        -- Stop moving once it settles on the floor
        if math.abs(vel.y) < 0.1 then
            self.object:set_velocity({x=0, y=0, z=0})
            self.object:set_acceleration({x=0, y=0, z=0})
            
            -- Optional: "Snap" rotation to the nearest 90 degrees so it looks like it landed on a face
            local rot = self.object:get_rotation()
            self.object:set_rotation({
                x = math.round(rot.x / (math.pi/2)) * (math.pi/2),
                y = math.round(rot.y / (math.pi/2)) * (math.pi/2),
                z = math.round(rot.z / (math.pi/2)) * (math.pi/2)
            })
        else
            -- Bounce slightly
            self.object:set_velocity({x = vel.x * 0.5, y = -vel.y * 0.3, z = vel.z * 0.5})
        end
    end
end,

Why this works:
 * The "Ideal 16-Die": Since the subset is random every time, you effectively have access to all 16 outcomes over many rolls, even though the physical object only has 6 faces at any given moment.
 * The Clatter: Two dice jumping at the same time with different velocities makes the box feel "alive."
 * Visual Polish: Snapping the rotation at the end makes it clear which "number" (or texture) won the roll.
Would you like me to add a "Clear" function where right-clicking the box removes the current dice so you can start a fresh roll?

Done! Adding a "Reset" or "Re-roll" feature makes the box much more playable. We’ll set it up so a right-click clears the old dice and spawns two fresh ones, while a punch (left-click) simply makes the existing dice "jump" and re-shuffle their textures.
I've also added a small on_destruct check so that if you dig the box, the dice don't stay floating in the air like ghosts of games past.
The Upgraded Dice Box
minetest.register_node("tool:dice_box", {
    description = "The Impossible Dice Box",
    drawtype = "nodebox",
    tiles = {"default_wood.png"},
    paramtype = "light",
    node_box = {
        type = "fixed",
        fixed = {
            {-0.5, -0.5, -0.5, 0.5, -0.4, 0.5}, -- Floor
            {-0.5, -0.4, -0.5, -0.4, 0.1, 0.5}, -- West Wall
            {0.4, -0.4, -0.5, 0.5, 0.1, 0.5},  -- East Wall
            {-0.4, -0.4, -0.5, 0.4, 0.1, -0.4}, -- South Wall
            {-0.4, -0.4, 0.4, 0.4, 0.1, 0.5},  -- North Wall
        },
    },

    -- Helper function to clear dice in this box
    on_rightclick = function(pos, node, clicker, itemstack)
        -- Find existing dice within the box's node space
        local objects = minetest.get_objects_inside_radius(pos, 0.7)
        for _, obj in ipairs(objects) do
            local ent = obj:get_luaentity()
            if ent and ent.name == "tool:impossible_die" then
                obj:remove()
            end
        end
        
        -- Spawn 2 New Dice
        for i = 1, 2 do
            local spawn_pos = {
                x = pos.x + (math.random(-15, 15) / 100), 
                y = pos.y - 0.2, -- Spawn slightly low so they 'pop' up
                z = pos.z + (math.random(-15, 15) / 100)
            }
            local ent = minetest.add_entity(spawn_pos, "tool:impossible_die")
            if ent then ent:get_luaentity():roll() end
        end
    end,

    -- Clean up dice when the box is removed
    on_destruct = function(pos)
        local objects = minetest.get_objects_inside_radius(pos, 0.7)
        for _, obj in ipairs(objects) do
            local ent = obj:get_luaentity()
            if ent and ent.name == "tool:impossible_die" then
                obj:remove()
            end
        end
    end,
})

The Physics Refinement
To make sure the dice stay contained even with horizontal randomness, we calculate the horizontal "kick" so it never exceeds the box walls (which are at ±0.4 from the center).
-- Add this to your tool:impossible_die "roll" function
local vx = (math.random() - 0.5) * 2.0 -- Speed between -1 and 1
local vz = (math.random() - 0.5) * 2.0
local vy = 2.5 + math.random() -- Random jump height

self.object:set_velocity({x=vx, y=vy, z=vz})

The Fix for on_step
The error is likely in how the "settling" logic was structured. Here is the corrected, syntax-safe on_step function for your tool:impossible_die entity:
    on_step = function(self, dtime)
        local pos = self.object:get_pos()
        local vel = self.object:get_velocity()

        -- 1. Identify the box position (integer coordinates)
        local box_pos = {
            x = math.floor(pos.x + 0.5), 
            y = math.floor(pos.y), 
            z = math.floor(pos.z + 0.5)
        }
        
        local node = minetest.get_node(box_pos)

        -- 2. Logic: If inside the box and touching the "floor" (y ~ -0.4)
        if node.name == "tool:dice_box" and pos.y <= (box_pos.y - 0.35) then
            -- If it's moving slowly enough, stop it entirely
            if math.abs(vel.y) < 0.2 then
                self.object:set_velocity({x=0, y=0, z=0})
                self.object:set_acceleration({x=0, y=0, z=0})
                
                -- 3. Snap Rotation: Align to 90-degree increments
                local rot = self.object:get_rotation()
                local snap = function(r)
                    return math.floor((r / (math.pi/2)) + 0.5) * (math.pi/2)
                end
                
                self.object:set_rotation({
                    x = snap(rot.x),
                    y = snap(rot.y),
                    z = snap(rot.z)
                })
            else
                -- 4. Simple Bounce: Reverse Y velocity with a dampening factor
                self.object:set_velocity({
                    x = vel.x * 0.5, 
                    y = -vel.y * 0.3, 
                    z = vel.z * 0.5
                })
            end
        end
    end,

That’s progress! It sounds like the "spawn and jump" logic is firing correctly, but the physical scale and world interaction (collision) are ignoring your changes.
In Minetest, the physical size of an entity and its visual size are controlled by different properties. Changing the collisionbox affects where it hits things, but it won't change how big the die looks, and it won't stop it from falling through the floor unless it’s actually colliding with the world.
1. Fix the Size (Visual + Physical)
To make the dice 0.1 in length, you need to set the visual_size and match the collisionbox to that same scale.
minetest.register_entity("tool:impossible_die", {
    visual = "cube",
    -- Visual size scales the model. Default is {x=1, y=1, z=1}.
    -- For a 0.1 sized die:
    visual_size = {x=0.1, y=0.1, z=0.1},
    
    -- Collision box is {min_x, min_y, min_z, max_x, max_y, max_z}
    -- This must be small to match your 0.1 die.
    collisionbox = {-0.05, -0.05, -0.05, 0.05, 0.05, 0.05},
    
    -- This makes it actually hit nodes in the world!
    physical = true,
    collide_with_objects = true,

2. Fix the "Falling Through Everything"
If they are falling through the floor, it's usually because physical = true is missing, or the on_step logic is overriding the engine's physics too aggressively.
Let's simplify the on_step so the engine handles the floor collision, and we only intervene to "snap" it once it stops moving.
    on_step = function(self, dtime)
        local vel = self.object:get_velocity()
        
        -- If moving very slowly, stop it and snap rotation
        if math.abs(vel.x) < 0.1 and math.abs(vel.y) < 0.1 and math.abs(vel.z) < 0.1 then
            self.object:set_velocity({x=0, y=0, z=0})
            self.object:set_acceleration({x=0, y=0, z=0})
            
            local rot = self.object:get_rotation()
            local snap = function(r)
                return math.floor((r / (math.pi/2)) + 0.5) * (math.pi/2)
            end
            self.object:set_rotation({x=snap(rot.x), y=snap(rot.y), z=snap(rot.z)})
        end
    end,

3. The "Jettison" Adjustment
Since the dice are now tiny (0.1), the jump velocity of 3 might look like they're being launched by a Tom and Jerry style spring-loaded trap! You might want to lower the vy in your roll function to something like 1.0 or 1.5.
Why visual_size is the key
In Minetest, textures are applied to the faces of the visual. If you don't define visual_size, it defaults to 1 \times 1 \times 1, which is the size of a full node. By setting it to 0.1, you're shrinking the "impossible die" to the scrap-of-paper scale you're likely looking for.

I see exactly what's happening. In your minetest.register_entity code, you updated the collisionbox, but you didn't actually tell the engine to scale the 3D model down. In Minetest, the visual (the 3D cube) defaults to 1 \times 1 \times 1 unless you explicitly set the visual_size.
Since the visual model is still size 1 but the collision box is tiny (0.1), the dice look huge and "ghost" through each other because their physical hitboxes are much smaller than the wood blocks you see.
The Fix: Adding visual_size
You need to add visual_size = {x = 0.1, y = 0.1, z = 0.1} to the entity registration. I also noticed that in your roll function, you are calling set_properties to update the textures, but set_properties overwrites any properties not included in the call. If you don't include the size in the roll function's set_properties, they might revert to full size when you roll them!
Update your entity registration like this:
minetest.register_entity("tool:impossible_die", {
    visual = "cube",
    -- This makes the model 0.1 size on startup
    visual_size = {x = 0.1, y = 0.1, z = 0.1},
    textures = {"wood01.png^dice_1.png", "wood01.png^dice_2.png", "wood01.png^dice_3.png", "wood01.png^dice_4.png", "wood01.png^dice_5.png", "wood01.png^dice_6.png"},
    collisionbox = {-0.05, -0.05, -0.05, 0.05, 0.05, 0.05},
    physical = true,
    collide_with_objects = true,

    on_activate = function(self, staticdata)
        self:roll()
    end,

    roll = function(self)
        local new_faces = get_random_six(die_pool)
        -- CRITICAL: Re-apply the visual_size here so it doesn't reset to 1x1x1
        self.object:set_properties({
            textures = new_faces,
            visual_size = {x = 0.1, y = 0.1, z = 0.1},
        })
        
        -- Add horizontal randomness so they don't overlap in the center
        local vx = (math.random() - 0.5) * 1.5
        local vz = (math.random() - 0.5) * 1.5
        
        self.object:set_velocity({x = vx, y = 2, z = vz})
        self.object:set_acceleration({x = 0, y = -9.8, z = 0})
    end,

    on_punch = function(self, puncher)
        self:roll()
    end,
})

Why they were overlapping
Because the collisionbox was 0.1 but the visual was 1.0, the "real" dice (the hitboxes) were bouncing off each other correctly, but the "ghost" images (the 1x1x1 cubes) were overlapping by 0.9 units. Now that the visual matches the hitbox, they should clatter against each other like real dice.
A Small Physics Tweak
In your on_rightclick for the dice_box, you have y = pos.y - 0.2. If your box floor is at -0.4, spawning at -0.2 might actually be spawning them inside the wooden floor of the box. Try changing it to y = pos.y + 0.1 so they drop into the box or pop up from the surface correctly.

[They are still sometimes overlapping, but it might not matter. Can we have so that when I left click the entity of one of the dice (if they overlap, say) it sends that very dice in the direction I'm pointing, (like a knockback) just like it was another roll, but the one I hit actually stays exactly the same die.]

That’s a great idea. It adds a bit of tactile "poking" to the box—perfect for when the dice get stuck in a corner or, as you said, overlap. It's like Tom poking at a trap with a stick to see if it’s still live!
The logic for this is actually quite elegant. When you "punch" (left-click) an entity, Minetest passes the puncher object. We can grab that player's look direction and use it to calculate a vector to "shove" the die.
The "Knockback" Logic
To keep the die exactly the same (no texture change), we simply omit the get_random_six call in a new function or a conditional check within on_punch.
Here is how to update your entity registration:
minetest.register_entity("tool:impossible_die", {
    -- ... [keep your visual, textures, and visual_size settings from before] ...

    -- This is your existing roll logic (which changes textures)
    roll = function(self)
        local new_faces = get_random_six(die_pool)
        self.object:set_properties({
            textures = new_faces,
            visual_size = {x = 0.1, y = 0.1, z = 0.1},
        })
        -- Standard jump
        self.object:set_velocity({x = (math.random()-0.5), y = 2, z = (math.random()-0.5)})
        self.object:set_acceleration({x = 0, y = -9.8, z = 0})
    end,

    -- This handles the Left-Click (Punch)
    on_punch = function(self, puncher)
        if not puncher then return end
        
        -- 1. Get the direction the player is looking
        local dir = puncher:get_look_dir()
        
        -- 2. Calculate "Knockback"
        -- We multiply the look direction by a force (e.g., 3.0) 
        -- and add a slight upward "pop" (y = 1.5) so it doesn't just slide
        local force = 3.0
        local velocity = {
            x = dir.x * force,
            y = 1.5, 
            z = dir.z * force
        }

        -- 3. Apply the shove WITHOUT changing textures
        self.object:set_velocity(velocity)
        self.object:set_acceleration({x = 0, y = -9.8, z = 0})

        -- 4. Add a random spin so it actually 'rolls' again
        self.object:set_rotation({
            x = math.random() * math.pi,
            y = math.random() * math.pi,
            z = math.random() * math.pi
        })
    end,
})

Why this fixes the overlap
By using the player's look_dir, you aren't just giving it a random jump; you are physically pushing it away from you. If two dice are overlapping, punching one will launch it in the direction you're facing, naturally separating them.
A Small Physics Detail: collide_with_objects
You mentioned they still overlap sometimes. In Minetest, collide_with_objects = true tells the engine to try and resolve collisions, but with very small entities (0.1 size), they can sometimes "phase" into each other if they land at the exact same time.
If you want them to be even more "solid," ensure your on_step function isn't setting the velocity to {x=0, y=0, z=0} too early. If they are still moving even slightly, the engine's collision solver has a better chance of pushing them apart.
